Grades 9-12
The general aim of the United Synagogue Youth program is to bring about a meaningful and fully reciprocal encounter of
Juadism, the Jewish people, and the synagogue on one side, and the Jewish teenager on the other. As a result of this encounter,
the Jewish teenager will, firstly, demonstrate and experience how the Jewish way of living, through study, action and fellowship
leads the way to personal fulfillment and growth while meeting his spiritual and social needs; and secondly, make a significant
contribution to his synagogue, community, society and the Jewish people.
For more information call the Youth office, 268-6736.
Mention the Center Yearbook When Patronizing Our Advertisers

===== PAGE 208 =====
The Afternoon Hebrew School of the Jacksonville Jew¬
ish Center is designed for students in grades 3-7 and
provides an elementary education leading to Bar/Bat
Mitzvah and continuation in the high school program.
Meeting twice during the week and on Saturdays, “the
basics” are at the core of the curriculum, with stress on
Hebrew reading, Jewish Social Studies, and current
events relating to Israel. Synagogue skills, holiday obser¬
vances and knowledge of prayers are all part of the
comprehensive Afternoon Hebrew School program.
Afternoon School

TO OUR ADVERTISERS:
Our constant gratitude, not only for making the publication possible, but also for the
support they lend to our programs. We urge our members to reciprocate with their
patronage.
Facts About the Center Yearbook
• A reference and guide for the Jacksonville Jewish Center membership and the
Jewish community.
• Serves over 7,000 members and advertisers.
• All proceeds devoted to the Center’s program.
The Yearbook is a summary of the various activities and programs of this Synagogue-
Center depicted in pictures and words. We are grateful to the many organizations of
this community and congregants who have cooperated in providing us with material
used.
We appreciate the efforts of our staff and other members of the Center who have
devoted time and effort on behalf of our 1988-89 Center Yearbook.
ST. MARKS

Brief Scope of Activities:
I H i H
'ISSiBSSk It
¡HHI
David Levin
Catering/
Food Services Director
Religious Services Traditional prayer services are held daily, morning and evening in the Witten Chapel. Friday evening
services, Sabbath and holiday services are observed throughout the entire year.
Personal Religious Observances — Traditional Jewish customs are observed: Circumcision, Naming of Girls, Pidyon
Ha-ben, Bar Mitzvah, Bat Mitzvah, Confirmation, Marriages, Conversion to Judaism, Bereavement.
Education — Daily Kindergarten and Nursery & Day Care with outstanding programs of secular and religious content.
Hebrew school, carefully graded with intensive Hebrew content, including Jewish history and customs, Sunday School for
kindergarten, first and second grades: Solomon Schechter Day School, a graded secular and Hebrew School, 1st through
7th grades; Hebrew High School, and Junior Congregations.
Extension Service — Library, outstanding collection of juvenile and adult Jewish books; Adult Education, religious and
cultural Jewish courses; music programs of religious and cultural Jewish music; P.T.A.; Sisterhood; Family Council, 55+,
social activities provided by Mr. and Mrs. Club, Single Adults; Family Recreation Program, summer weekdays and Sundays
for all ages.
Youth Activities — ATID for college age youth; United Synagogue Youth, Kadima, Chalutzim, Boy Scouts, Cub Scouts,
Girl Scouts, Brownies; Sunday Funday; athletics, programs for youth and adults; Center Day Camp and summer program
at our 36 acre site.
Family Recreation program - Center Campsite . . . swimming, athletics, snack bar; available for members during the
summer months. Campsite includes olympic-size swimming pool, 2 tennis courts, baseball, soccer and football fields and
playground.
For additional information, call the Center office — 268-6736.

Early Childhood Department
I am honored to be serving as Director of the Jacksonville Jewish Center
Early Childhood Department at this most exciting time in the school’s history.
We are going through a period of unprecedented growth both in enrollment
and facilities.
As we celebrate this transition to a new stage in the life of our school, we
also pause to consider and acknowledge the roots from which we have grown.
While we are proud of our school at Third and Silver Streets and were enthu¬
siastic about our move to Crown Point Road twelve years ago, we are excep¬
tionally proud of our school’s new building growth and position in the com¬
munity.
We feel we have succeeded in enhancing Jewish identity and transmitting it
to many generations. We believe the Jacksonville Jewish Center Early Child¬
hood Department, with the continued support of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center congregation, will become increasingly important to these families
Marilyn Sandler who desire a quality Jewish preschool.
Throughout the school’s history, people have stepped forward to contribute their time, energy and
resources whenever they were needed. We are today blessed with a broad base of support in the Jew¬
ish community, as well as an incredibly talented and diverse group of parents, who have invested their
most precious resources — their children — in our institution.
Our survival as a Jewish people ultimately depends on how well we teach our children.
It is rewarding to me to be able to spend my time on this most worthwhile endeavor. Participating
in a school which is continually “investing in excellence” is an exciting and energizing experience.
Shirley Bielski
Administrative
Assistant
Pre-school Activities

Center Day Camp
Boardwalk
& Baseball
Punk Day
’88
TOGETHER ... we learned, we
played, experienced and we grew.
We traveled to Orlando’s Board¬
walk and Baseball, Wild Waters
and Mayport. We bowled, putt
putted, skated and rode ponies.
We learned to swim, passed Red
Cross beginners, advanced begin¬
ners and a whole lot more. We
swam for 30 minutes raising money
for the pool, $450 for the Swim-a-
thon to be exact.
Trail mix, s’mores, banana cream
pies and blueberry ice cream are
among our specialties. Campouts,
volleyball, free swim, Judaica and
computers were among our
favorites.
We met police officers, firemen,
karate experts, magicians and a
juggler. We even met the construc¬
tion workers and saw their
machines.
Campouts
are fun!
We dressed up like punks and
doctors, cartoon characters and
bandits. Each costume made with
our own creative touch.

Adult Education
Expansion is taking place . . .
...Jewish mind expansion that is! Adult education has become an integral part of
the ongoing activities of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. During the year new
classes and groups for study have been meeting regularly. Whether it was
attendance at a Hebrew class, the Sisterhood Bar/Bat Mitzvah class, the
Shabbaton weekend, a book review or holiday workshops, our members came
together to grow Jewishly. They thus lent testimony to the fact that men and
women of all ages in our congregation are interested in becoming better
informed Jews.
As we look to the new year in terms of adult education, there is reason to feel
excited. Stimulating speakers for the Shabbaton weekends are going to be
visiting and sharing their expertise with us. Mini-sessions are being planned as
well as the popular Hebrew classes. Most importantly, however, one of the most
basic tenets of Judaism, the importance of learning, is not only being acknow¬
ledged but it is being given a life of its own at the Center.
This year Lillie Ray Levy will be chairing the Adult Education committee. She
would appreciate your help, comments or suggestions. If you would like to serve
on the committee, call Lillie Ray at 260-2534.
Our sincere thanks to Marilyn and Mike Mass
and their committee for coordinating the
Shabbaton featuring Dr. Morton Siegel,
(pictured).
In June, Senator Stephen Solarz was the speaker
for the annual Setzer-Levit Lecture.
Senator Solarz brought out hundreds of people
to hear him discuss Israel's politics.

JACKSONVILLE JEWISH CENTER MASTER CALENDAR 1988-89
===== PAGE 245 =====
The Jewish Center’s Recreation Department’s goals are to provide the Jewish community
with program and activities that promote the improvement of physical skills, health, the
development of special interest and/or hobbies, and to provide the opportunity for relaxation
and social camaraderie.
Many of the recreation activities take place at the Center’s
Recreation Park which consists of approximately 10 acres of
beautifully wooded campgrounds, complete with an olympic-size
swimming pool, bath houses, tennis courts, softball fields, and
outdoor basketball court, badminton area, children’s playground,
gazebo, snack bar and shaded picnic area.
Within the main building is a regulation basketball court, the
fully-equipped Neal Portnoy Youth Lounge and an arts and crafts
room, a large room for dances and a versatile stage for musical and
dramatic productions and a meat and dairy kitchen with the most
modern equipment. We take pride in our recreation program and the
marvelous facilities of our Center.
Gayle Bailys will serve as Recreation Director. We are looking
forward to a successful year with Gayle at the helm.
Gayle Bailys

From the Executive Director
As the New Year approaches it is hard to believe a year has gone by. llene, Allison and I
settled into our new home and community and found Jacksonville to be everything we hoped it
would be and more. We have made many new friends and find ourselves actively involved in the
growth of the Jacksonville Jewish Community.
The past year has been a very busy one. We embarked on a dynamic building program that
involved much time coordinating activities to continue as usual throughout the project. Although
the building is not yet complete, the members of the Center have much to be proud of. We also
have much to look forward to. Our new synagogue/school campus will be one of the most dy¬
namic of its kind in the country.
With the help and support of our Sisterhood and Center Board of Directors, my recommenda¬
tion to install Desktop Publishing computers in our offices was accomplished. Although we are still
in the training stage with the system, you will begin to see the Bulletin and other graphics being
produced directly in our office. Desktop Publishing will give us the ability to be flexible and profes¬
sional with our Bulletin and other printed materials, while at the same time save the Center a
considerable sum of money.
As you know Blanche Slott retired this summer as Center Caterer.
An exhaustive search was made both in our area and across the nation to find the right and talented person to fill this
difficult role. We have recently found that person.
I am proud to welcome David Levin to the Center as Caterer/Food Service Director. David joins our staff with lifetime of
experiences in the food business. David has worked at the Golden Pheasant in Tallahassee and most recently at Epping Forest
here in Jacksonville. David comes to us at a very opportune time. Our kitchen is about to be opened following an extensive
renovation. The new meeting rooms being built will provide a perfect location for some of the smaller luncheons and dinners
which we have never had the proper setting at the Center. Help me in welcoming David, Gail, and his daughters, Rachel and
Claudia, to our Center family. We are truly at a new beginning.
Our building will be one of the most dynamic synagogue Centers in the country. It gives us, the professional staff the
opportunity to lead this congregation to greater heights. Our programs will always be centered around the learning of Torah and
life cycle events. We hope, with your participation, we can lead our congregation in new avenues. We look forward to reaching
our common goal.
My wife llene, and daughter Allison, join me in wishing you all a healthy and happy New Year.
L’Shana Tova Tikatavu.
Eric G. Reiter
Eric G. Reiter

===== PAGE 253 =====
The Family Council, which came into being
this past year, reaches out to mothers and fa¬
thers of present and future students in all of
the Jacksonville Jewish Center’s educational
programs. It seeks to increase parental in¬
volvement in the learning process.
Some Center parents are privileged to watch
their children build a reservoir of knowledge
about their heritage that is running deeper
than their own. But on the other side of this
coin i$ the consequent realization that rein¬
forcement at home of these Jewish values and
traditions may be missing or incomplete. The
best of intentions cannot make up for weak¬
nesses in the education level attained by the
parents.
In the course of the year the Family Council
will be sponsoring many activities designed for
parental involvement. Even when the parents
are knowledgeable and observant, their atten¬
dance at these functions will be a message to
their children that their mothers and fathers
care about what they are learning, and believe
in it.
Henry Blumenthal
1988-89 Officers
Henry Blumenthal, chairman; Sue Ann
Blumenthal, secretary; Sheree Spriggs,
treasurer; Jane Grann, publicity; Peggy Or-
ganes and Ellen Rubens, programs; Kathie
Wallach, membership; and Beverly
Bamhard, art.
